# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

45-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of how Prometheus metrics are registered and exposed across the three repositories. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed findings on Prometheus metric registration patterns across **kubernetes/kubernetes**, **grafana/grafana**, and **prometheus/prometheus**:

### Key Findings:

**Kubernetes** uses a custom metrics wrapper framework with:
- Central global registry in `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go`
- Wrapper types (`metrics.NewCounter`, `metrics.NewGauge`, etc.) that extend Prometheus metrics with stability tracking
- `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` for registration

**Grafana** uses the standard Prometheus client library directly with:
- Registration functions that accept `prometheus.Registerer` as parameters
- Flexible design allowing different registries
- Pattern: `RegisterJobMetrics(registry)`, `RegisterQueueMetrics(registry)` in `pkg/registry/apis/provisioning/jobs/metrics.go`

**Prometheus** uses constructor-based metric initialization with:
- Functions like `newScrapeMetrics(reg)` and `NewManagerMetrics(registerer)` that handle both creation and registration
- Explicit error handling in loops rather than panic-on-error
- Built-in `Unregister()` methods for proper lifecycle management

The answer file includes 18 representative files and 18 key symbols showing these patterns, plus a detailed narrative explanation of the architectural differences and tradeoffs between the three approaches.

wrapper framework** built on top of the Prometheus client library:\\n\\n- **Central Registry**: The global registry is defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go` custom types (`metrics.NewCounter()`, `metrics.NewGauge()`, `metrics.NewHistogram()`) defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/counter.go`, `gauge.go`, and `histogram.go`. These wrappers extend Prometheus metrics with stability level tracking.\\n\\n- **Registration Pattern**: Metrics are registered using `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` for standard metrics or `legacyregistry.CustomMustRegister()` for custom collectors. The registry is initialized in `init()` with process and Go collectors.\\n\\n- **Key Files**:\\n  - `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go` - Global registry definition\\n  - `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/counter.go` - Counter wrapper implementation\\n  - `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/gauge.go` - Gauge wrapper implementation\\n  - `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/histogram.go` - Histogram wrapper implementation\\n  - `pkg/controller/job/metrics/metrics.go` - Example registration using `Register()` with `sync.Once` guard\\n  - `pkg/controller/nodelifecycle/metrics.go` - Example registration pattern\\n\\n### Grafana (grafana/grafana)\\n\\nGrafana uses the **standard Prometheus client library directly** with registration functions:\\n\\n- **Metric Creation**: Metrics are created using standard Prometheus functions (`prometheus.NewCounter()`, `prometheus.NewGauge()`, `prometheus.NewHistogram()` and their Vec variants).\\n\\n- **Registration Pattern**: Metric registration happens through dedicated registration functions that accept `prometheus.Registerer` as a parameter. These functions create the metrics and immediately register them with `registry.MustRegister()`. This pattern allows flexibility in using different registries.\\n\\n- **Key Files**:\\n  - `pkg/infra/metrics/metrics.go` - Defines global metric variables but doesn't register them\\n  - `pkg/registry/apis/provisioning/jobs/metrics.go` - Registration functions `RegisterJobMetrics()` and `RegisterQueueMetrics()` that take a registerer parameter\\n  - `pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/prometheus_metrics_middleware.go` - Example of `Register()` and `MustRegister()` methods that work with a provided registerer\\n  - `pkg/registry/apis/provisioning/controller/metrics.go` - Registration function with metrics creation inside `registerFinalizerMetrics()`\\n  - `pkg/services/auth/idimpl/metrics.go` - Pattern of checking `if reg != nil` before registering\\n\\n### Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus)\\n\\nPrometheus uses **constructor functions that return metrics structs** with explicit registration:\\n\\n- **Metric Creation and Registration**: Metrics are created with `prometheus.New*()` functions inside constructor functions (e.g., `newScrapeMetrics()`, `NewManagerMetrics()`) that take a `prometheus.Registerer` parameter.\\n\\n- **Registration Pattern**: Metrics are collected in a slice and registered in a loop with error handling. The function returns both the metrics struct and an error. This provides better control and error reporting compared to panic-on-error approaches.\\n\\n- **Unregistration Support**: Many metric structs include an `Unregister()` method to clean up metrics when they're no longer needed, demonstrating proper lifecycle management.\\n\\n- **Key Files**:\\n  - `scrape/metrics.go` - `newScrapeMetrics()` function that creates and registers ~20 metrics with explicit error handling loop (lines 266-303)\\n  - `discovery/metrics.go` - `NewManagerMetrics()` function demonstrating the pattern with metrics creation followed by registration loop and error handling\\n  - `notifier/metric.go` - Metric creation and registration for alerting\\n  - `storage/remote/queue_manager.go` - Metrics creation in constructor\\n  - `tsdb/db.go` - Database metrics registration\\n  - `tsdb/head.go` - Head metrics using `prometheus.NewGaugeFunc()` for dynamic values\\n  - `rules/group.go` - Rule group metrics\\n  - `discovery/kubernetes/metrics.go` - Kubernetes discovery metrics\\n\\n### Key Differences and Patterns\\n\\n1. **Registry Management**:\\n   - Kubernetes: Central global registry with custom wrapper\\n   - Grafana: Flexible registration with provided registerer parameter\\n   - Prometheus: Constructor pattern with explicit error handling\\n\\n2. **Error Handling**:\\n   - Kubernetes: Uses `MustRegister()` which panics on error\\n   - Grafana: Uses `MustRegister()` or `Register()` with panic/error returns\\n   - Prometheus: Explicit loop with error wrapping and return\\n\\n3. **Initialization Timing**:\\n   - Kubernetes: Metrics created at package init time, registered separately via functions\\n   - Grafana: Metrics created on demand when registration functions are called\\n   - Prometheus: Both creation and registration happen in constructor functions\\n\\n4. **Unregistration Support**:\\n   - Kubernetes: No explicit unregistration (global registry)\\n   - Grafana: Limited unregistration support\\n   - Prometheus: Explicit `Unregister()` methods for lifecycle management\\n\\nAll three projects use the same underlying Prometheus client library (`github.com/prometheus/client_golang/prometheus`) but with different abstraction levels and registration strategies suited to their architectural needs.\"\n}\n",

custom types (`metrics.NewCounter()`, `metrics.NewGauge()`, `metrics.NewHistogram()`) defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/counter.go`, `gauge.go`, and `histogram.go`. These wrappers extend Prometheus metrics with stability level tracking.\\n\\n- **Registration Pattern**: Metrics are registered using `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` for standard metrics or `legacyregistry.CustomMustRegister()` for custom collectors. The registry is initialized in `init()` with process and Go collectors.\\n\\n- **Key Files**:\\n  - `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go` - Global registry definition\\n  - `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/counter.go` - Counter wrapper implementation\\n  - `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/gauge.go` - Gauge wrapper implementation\\n  - `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/histogram.go` - Histogram wrapper implementation\\n  - `pkg/controller/job/metrics/metrics.go` - Example registration using `Register()` with `sync.Once` guard\\n  - `pkg/controller/nodelifecycle/metrics.go` - Example registration pattern\\n\\n### Grafana (grafana/grafana)\\n\\nGrafana uses the **standard Prometheus client library directly** with registration functions:\\n\\n- **Metric Creation**: Metrics are created using standard Prometheus functions (`prometheus.NewCounter()`, `prometheus.NewGauge()`, `prometheus.NewHistogram()` and their Vec variants).\\n\\n- **Registration Pattern**: Metric registration happens through dedicated registration functions that accept `prometheus.Registerer` as a parameter. These functions create the metrics and immediately register them with `registry.MustRegister()`. This pattern allows flexibility in using different registries.\\n\\n- **Key Files**:\\n  - `pkg/infra/metrics/metrics.go` - Defines global metric variables but doesn't register them\\n  - `pkg/registry/apis/provisioning/jobs/metrics.go` - Registration functions `RegisterJobMetrics()` and `RegisterQueueMetrics()` that take a registerer parameter\\n  - `pkg/infra/httpclient/httpclientprovider/prometheus_metrics_middleware.go` - Example of `Register()` and `MustRegister()` methods that work with a provided registerer\\n  - `pkg/registry/apis/provisioning/controller/metrics.go` - Registration function with metrics creation inside `registerFinalizerMetrics()`\\n  - `pkg/services/auth/idimpl/metrics.go` - Pattern of checking `if reg != nil` before registering\\n\\n### Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus)\\n\\nPrometheus uses **constructor functions that return metrics structs** with explicit registration:\\n\\n- **Metric Creation and Registration**: Metrics are created with `prometheus.New*()` functions inside constructor functions (e.g., `newScrapeMetrics()`, `NewManagerMetrics()`) that take a `prometheus.Registerer` parameter.\\n\\n- **Registration Pattern**: Metrics are collected in a slice and registered in a loop with error handling. The function returns both the metrics struct and an error. This provides better control and error reporting compared to panic-on-error approaches.\\n\\n- **Unregistration Support**: Many metric structs include an `Unregister()` method to clean up metrics when they're no longer needed, demonstrating proper lifecycle management.\\n\\n- **Key Files**:\\n  - `scrape/metrics.go` - `newScrapeMetrics()` function that creates and registers ~20 metrics with explicit error handling loop (lines 266-303)\\n  - `discovery/metrics.go` - `NewManagerMetrics()` function demonstrating the pattern with metrics creation followed by registration loop and error handling\\n  - `notifier/metric.go` - Metric creation and registration for alerting\\n  - `storage/remote/queue_manager.go` - Metrics creation in constructor\\n  - `tsdb/db.go` - Database metrics registration\\n  - `tsdb/head.go` - Head metrics using `prometheus.NewGaugeFunc()` for dynamic values\\n  - `rules/group.go` - Rule group metrics\\n  - `discovery/kubernetes/metrics.go` - Kubernetes discovery metrics\\n\\n### Key Differences and Patterns\\n\\n1. **Registry Management**:\\n   - Kubernetes: Central global registry with custom wrapper\\n   - Grafana: Flexible registration with provided registerer parameter\\n   - Prometheus: Constructor pattern with explicit error handling\\n\\n2. **Error Handling**:\\n   - Kubernetes: Uses `MustRegister()` which panics on error\\n   - Grafana: Uses `MustRegister()` or `Register()` with panic/error returns\\n   - Prometheus: Explicit loop with error wrapping and return\\n\\n3. **Initialization Timing**:\\n   - Kubernetes: Metrics created at package init time, registered separately via functions\\n   - Grafana: Metrics created on demand when registration functions are called\\n   - Prometheus: Both creation and registration happen in constructor functions\\n\\n4. **Unregistration Support**:\\n   - Kubernetes: No explicit unregistration (global registry)\\n   - Grafana: Limited unregistration support\\n   - Prometheus: Explicit `Unregister()` methods for lifecycle management\\n\\nAll three projects use the same underlying Prometheus client library (`github.com/prometheus/client_golang/prometheus`) but with different abstraction levels and registration strategies suited to their architectural needs.\"\n}\n",
  "filePath": "/workspace/answer.json",
